                        cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="#"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=&amp;md5=9874b665cc7a056b8e2f928dd3112440</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit8" data-doi="10.1007/s40820-020-00562-7"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Quan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Dimensional Gradient Structure of CoSe<sub>2</sub>@CNTs-MXene Anode Assisted by Ether for High-Capacity, Stable Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Nano-Micro Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>13</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">40</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1007/s40820-020-00562-7</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D13%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D40%26journal%3DNano-Micro%2BLett.%26author%3DE.%2BXu%26author%3DP.%2BLi%26author%3DJ.%2BQuan%26author%3DH.%2BZhu%26author%3DL.%2BWang%26author%3DY.%2BChang%26author%3DZ.%2BSun%26author%3DL.%2BChen%26author%3DD.%2BYu%26author%3DY.%2BJiang%26title%3DDimensional%2BGradient%2BStructure%2Bof%2BCoSe2%2540CNTs-MXene%2BAnode%2BAssisted%2Bby%2BEther%2Bfor%2BHigh-Capacity%252C%2BStable%2BSodium%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1007%252Fs40820-020-00562-7&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c20154&amp;doiOfLink=10.1007%2Fs40820-020-00562-7&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Dimensional Gradient Structure of CoSe2@CNTs-MXene Anode Assisted by Ether for High-Capacity, Stable Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu Enze; Li Pengcheng; Quan Junjie; Zhu Hanwen; Sun Zhenjie; Chen Lei; Jiang Yang; Wang Li; Chang Yajing; Yu Dabin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano-micro letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">40</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Recently, abundant resources, low-cost sodium-ion batteries are deemed to the new-generation battery in the field of large-scale energy storage.  Nevertheless, poor active reaction dynamics, dissolution of intermediates and electrolyte matching problems are significant challenges that need to be solved.  Herein, dimensional gradient structure of sheet-tube-dots is constructed with CoSe2@CNTs-MXene.  Gradient structure is conducive to fast migration of electrons and ions with the association of ether electrolyte.  For half-cell, CoSe2@CNTs-MXene exhibits high initial coulomb efficiency (81.7%) and excellent cycling performance (400 mAh g(-1) cycling for 200 times in 2 A g(-1)).  Phase transformation pathway from crystalline CoSe2-Na2Se with Co and then amorphous CoSe2 in the discharge/charge process is also explored by in situ X-ray diffraction.  Density functional theory study discloses the CoSe2@CNTs-MXene in ether electrolyte system which contributes to stable sodium storage performance owing to the strong adsorption force from hierarchical structure and weak interaction between electrolyte and electrode interface.  For full cell, CoSe2@CNTs-MXene//Na3V2 (PO4)3/C full battery can also afford a competitively reversible capacity of 280 mAh g(-1) over 50 cycles.  Concisely, profiting from dimensional gradient structure and matched electrolyte of CoSe2@CNTs-MXene hold great application potential for stable sodium storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcSNIXzBS4qhe5SWdIdmEou5fW6udTcc2ea8HOx1Fay8XLntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BB2c7pt1KrsQ%253D%253D&amp;md5=603abdedbec7d13e93c9c18e002f0fe1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit9" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2019.122206"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, X.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, H.                 10.1016/j.cej.2019.122206</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D378%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D122206%26journal%3DChem.%2BEng.%2BJ.%26author%3DB.%2BZhao%26author%3DQ.%2BLiu%26author%3DG.%2BWei%26author%3DJ.%2BWang%26author%3DX.-Y.%2BYu%26author%3DX.%2BLi%26author%3DH.%2BB.%2BWu%26title%3DSynthesis%2Bof%2BCoSe2%2BNanoparticles%2BEmbedded%2Bin%2BN-Doped%2BCarbon%2Bwith%2BConformal%2BTiO2%2BShell%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.cej.2019.122206&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c20154&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.cej.2019.122206&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synthesis of CoSe2 nanoparticles embedded in N-doped carbon with conformal TiO2 shell for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Bo; Liu, Qianqian; Wei, Guijuan; Wang, Jianghao; Yu, Xin-Yao; Li, Xiang; Wu, Hao Bin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">378</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">122206</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMEJAJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1385-8947</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">CoSe2 is a potential anode material for Na-ion batteries in terms of their high Na storage capacity and tunable properties.  However, structural degrdn. and unstable interphase during the reversible sodiation and de-sodiation lead to fast capacity decay.  The authors develop a nanocomposite architecture based on CoSe2 nanoparticles embedded in N-doped C matrix with conformal TiO2 coating (CoSe2@NC@TiO2) by using a metal-org. framework-assisted strategy.  The small CoSe2 nanoparticles and N-doped C matrix facilitate charge transport and suppress the structural degrdn., while the redox-active TiO2 shell further strengthens the structural and interfacial stability without decreasing the capacity.  The as-prepd. CoSe2@NC@TiO2 nanocomposite particles deliver a reversible Na storage capacity of 520 mA-h g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 with a capacity retention of 78% after 200 cycles, in contrast to the rapid capacity fading after 50 cycles of the pristine CoSe2@NC particles without TiO2 shell.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqouUiE8HspjrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg-a7i-jEvDpA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Co-Construction of Sulfur Vacancies and Heterojunctions in Tungsten Disulfide to Induce Fast Electronic/Ionic Diffusion Kinetics for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yu; Qian, Ji; Zhang, Minghao; Wang, Shuo; Wang, Zhaohua; Li, Maosheng; Bai, Ying; An, Qinyou; Xu, Huajie; Wu, Feng; Mai, Liqiang; Wu, Chuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Engineering novel electrode materials with unique architectures has a significant impact on tuning the structural/electrochem. properties for boosting the performance of secondary battery systems.  Herein, starting from well-organized WS2 nanorods, an ingenious design of a one-step method is proposed to prep. a bimetallic sulfide composite with a coaxial carbon coating layer, simply enabled by ZIF-8 introduction. A great potential in practical application is also exhibited, where a full cell based on the WS2-x/ZnS@C anode and the P2-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn1/3O2 cathode can maintain a reversible capacity of 89.4 mAh g-1 after 500 cycles at 1 A g-1.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Heterostructures exhibit intriguing and significant properties for functional material applications, such as photosensing devices, semiconductor materials, and supercapacitors.  Rechargeable batteries as typical energy-storage devices have drawn widespread attention in the past several decades, on account of high energy d., being low-cost, and ecofriendly.  Prepg. superior active materials is the crit. technol. to ameliorate the electrochem. performance of batteries.  In recent years, the concept of constructing heterostructures for the application of electrode materials has been considered as a promising design approach.  Among all the electrode materials, metal chalcogenides (MCs) have presented excellent properties due to their high theor. capacity based on multielectron reaction.  Herein, the progress on MCs with heterostructures is summarized in terms of various material species and their specific application for several typical battery systems.  Finally, possible challenges and comprehensive perspectives are given to provide an instructive direction for the thoughtful design strategies of heterostructures and the development of MCs for next-generations rechargeable batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoN9-wvLvqD7bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg-a7i-jEvDpA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium-based dual-ion batteries via coupling high-capacity selenium/graphene anode with high-voltage graphite cathode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hou, Xiankun; Li, Wenhao; Wang, Yingying; Li, Shaofang; Meng, Yunfeng; Yu, Haiyue; Chen, Baokuan; Wu, Xinglong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chinese Chemical Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">31</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Dual ion batteries (DIBs) exhibit broad application prospects in the field of elec. energy storage (EES) devices with excellent properties, such as high voltage, high energy d., and low cost.  In the graphite-based DIBs, high voltage is needed to store enough anions with the formation of anion intercalation compd. XCn (X = AlCl-4, PF-6, TFSI-, etc.).  Hence, it is difficult for graphite-based DIBs to match proper anodes and electrolytes.  Here, an Se/graphene composite is prepd. via a convenient method, and assembled into a dual-ion full battery (DIFB) as anode with graphite cathode and 1 mol/L NaPF6 in EC:EMC (1:1, v:v).  This DIFB has achieved a high discharge capacity of 75.9 mA-h/g and high medium output voltage of 3.5 V at 0.1 A/g.  Actually, the suitable anode materials, such as the present Se/graphene composite, are extremely important for the development and application of graphite-based DIBs.  This study is enlightening for the design of future low-cost EES devices including graphite-based DIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpqej6qI-51gbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg-a7i-jEvDpA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXht1SrsL%252FO&amp;md5=2aa10bfaf42d934de6640795b316ec92</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202101137"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bahlawane, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, B.                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Review on conversion-alloying anode materials for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Fang, Libin; Bahlawane, Naoufal; Sun, Wenping; Pan, Hongge; Xu, Ben Bin; Yan, Mi; Jiang, Yinzhu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">17</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">37</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2101137</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The past decade has witnessed a rapidly growing interest toward sodium ion battery (SIB) for large-scale energy storage in view of the abundance and easy accessibility of sodium resources.  Key to addressing the remaining challenges and setbacks and to translate lab science into commercializable products is the development of high-performance anode materials.  Anode materials featuring combined conversion and alloying mechanisms are one of the most attractive candidates, due to their high theor. capacities and relatively low working voltages.  The current understanding of sodium-storage mechanisms in conversion-alloying anode materials is presented here.  The challenges faced by these materials in SIBs, and the corresponding improvement strategies, are comprehensively discussed in correlation with the resulting electrochem. behavior.  Finally, with the guidance and perspectives, a roadmap toward the development of advanced conversion-alloying materials for commercializable SIBs is created.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrrNAJqE0vUU7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljWygX8_5_Rrg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhslyksLjK&amp;md5=ba1adcae9d915929904905f95ab180fe</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201706668"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, X.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lou, X.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Strongly coupled 2D transition metal chalcogenide-MXene-carbonaceous nanoribbon heterostructures with ultrafast ion transport for boosting sodium/potassium ions storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cao, Junming; Li, Junzhi; Li, Dongdong; Yuan, Zeyu; Zhang, Yuming; Shulga, Valerii; Sun, Ziqi; Han, Wei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano-Micro Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">113</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NLAEBV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2150-5551</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nano-Micro Letters</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Combining with the advantages of two-dimensional (2D) nanomaterials, MXenes have shown great potential in next generation rechargeable batteries.  Similar with other 2D materials, MXenes generally suffer severe self-agglomeration, low capacity, and unsatisfied durability, particularly for larger sodium/potassium ions, compromising their practical values.  In this work, a novel ternary heterostructure self-assembled from transition metal selenides (MSe, M = Cu, Ni, and Co), MXene nanosheets and N-rich carbonaceous nanoribbons (CNRibs) with ultrafast ion transport properties is designed for sluggish sodium-ion (SIB) and potassium-ion (PIB) batteries.  Benefiting from the diverse chem. characteristics, the pos. charged MSe anchored onto the electroneg. hydroxy (-OH) functionalized MXene surfaces through electrostatic adsorption, while the fungal-derived CNRibs bonded with the other side of MXene through amino bridging and hydrogen bonds.  This unique MXene-based heterostructure prevents the restacking of 2D materials, increases the intrinsic cond., and most importantly, provides ultrafast interfacial ion transport pathways and extra surficial and interfacial storage sites, and thus, boosts the high-rate storage performances in SIB and PIB applications.  Both the quant. kinetic anal. and the d. functional theory (DFT) calcns. revealed that the interfacial ion transport is several orders higher than that of the pristine MXenes, which delivered much enhanced Na+ (536.3 mAh g-1@ 0.1 A g-1) and K+ (305.6 mAh g-1@ 1.0 A g-1) storage capabilities and excellent long-term cycling stability.  Therefore, this work provides new insights into 2D materials engineering and low-cost, but kinetically sluggish post-Li batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrgAD9dWM2p_bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljWygX8_5_Rrg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhvVOhsr3J&amp;md5=1199ef346ef23b4d8d8a6d66f28e482d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1016/j.cclet.2021.10.014"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lin, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Metal-Organic Frameworks Derived Carbon-Coated ZnSe/Co<sub>0.85</sub>Se@N-Doped Carbon Microcuboid as an Advanced Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chin.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Promoting Ge Alloying Reaction via Heterostructure Engineering for High Efficient and Ultra-Stable Sodium-Ion Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shang, Chaoqun; Hu, Le; Luo, Dan; Kempa, Krzysztof; Zhang, Yongguang; Zhou, Guofu; Wang, Xin; Chen, Zhongwei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Science (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">22</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2002358</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ASDCCF</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2198-3844</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Germanium-based materials have been considered as potential anode materials for sodium-ion batteries owing to their high theor. specific capacity.  However,poor cond. and Na+ diffusivity of Ge-based materials result in retardant ion/electron transportation and insufficient sodium storage efficiency, leading to sluggish reaction kinetics.  To intrinsically maximize sodium storage capability of Ge,nitrogen doped carbon-coated Cu3Ge/Ge heterostructure material is developed for enhanced sodium storage.  The pod-like structure of Cu3Ge/Ge-C exposes numerous active surface to shorten ion transportation pathway while uniform encapsulation of carbon shell improves electron transportation, leading to enhanced reaction kinetics.  Theor. calcn. reveals Cu3Ge/Ge heterostructure can offer decent electron conduction and lower Na+ diffusion barrier, which further promotes Ge alloying reaction and improves its sodium storage capability close to its theor. value.  In addn.,uniform encapsulation of nitrogen-doped carbon on Cu3Ge/Ge heterostructure material efficiently alleviates its vol. expansion and prevents its decompn., further ensuring its structural integrity upon cycling.  Attributed to these unique superiorities, as-prepd. Cu3Ge/Ge-C electrode demonstrates admirable discharge capacity, outstanding rate capability and prolonged cycle lifespan (178 mAh g-1 at 4.0 A g-1 after 4000 cycles).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpztoXHktbqurVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljWygX8_5_Rrg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXovVyqtLg%253D&amp;md5=018b4ec358c99ab3cda585d18b97d63b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1016/j.jechem.2020.06.066"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kong, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lv, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Integration of Cobalt Selenide Nanocrystals with Interlayer Expanded 3D Se/N Co-Doped Carbon Networks for Superior Sodium-Ion Storage</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Porous hollow α-Fe2O3@TiO2 core-shell nanospheres for superior lithium/sodium storage capability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Fu, Yanqing; Wei, Qiliang; Wang, Xianyou; Shu, Hongbo; Yang, Xiukang; Sun, Shuhui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Porous hollow α-Fe2O3@TiO2 core-shell nanospheres for use as anode materials in Li-ion batteries (LIBs) and Na-ion batteries (SIBs) were successfully fabricated by a simple template-assisted method, which was rarely reported before.  SEM, TEM and N2 adsorption-desorption isotherms reveal that the as-prepd. α-Fe2O3@TiO2 is composed of a hollow inner cavity and an outer shell with massive mesopores.  This porous hollow structure is capable of buffering the large vol. variation of α-Fe2O3 during cycling and preventing the electrode from pulverization and aggregation, as well as providing sufficiently large interstitial space within the crystallog. structure to host alkalis (Li and Na).  As a consequence, this hybrid composite exhibits outstanding electrochem. properties, e.g., high specific capacity, excellent cyclability, satisfactory rate performance, and splendid initial coulombic efficiency for both LIBs and SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpScMXwn2oVRLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj0aUOCMnZnNA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Designed Formation of Hybrid Nanobox Composed of Carbon Sheathed CoSe2 Anchored on Nitrogen-Doped Carbon Skeleton as Ultrastable Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Baoqiang; Liu, Yi; Jin, Xu; Jiao, Shuhong; Wang, Gongrui; Peng, Bo; Zeng, Suyuan; Shi, Liang; Li, Jianming; Zhang, Genqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Research on Na-ion batteries (SIBs) has recently been revitalized due to the unique features of much lower costs and comparable energy/power d. to Li-ion batteries (LIBs), which holds great potential for grid-level energy storage systems.  Transition metal dichalcogenides (TMDCs) are considered as promising anode candidates for SIBs with high theor. capacity, while their intrinsic low elec. cond. and large vol. expansion upon Na+ intercalation raise the challenging issues of poor cycle stability and inferior rate performance.  Herein, the designed formation of hybrid nanoboxes composed of C-protected CoSe2 nanoparticles anchored on N-doped C hollow skeletons (denoted as CoSe2@C∩NC) via a template-assisted refluxing process followed by conventional selenization treatment is reported, which exhibits tremendously enhanced electrochem. performance when applied as the anode for SIBs.  Specifically, it can deliver a high reversible specific capacity of 324 mA-h g-1 at c.d. of 0.1 A g-1 after 200 cycles and exhibit outstanding high rate cycling stability at the rate of 5 A g-1 over 2000 cycles.  This work provides a rational strategy for the design of advanced hybrid nanostructures as anode candidates for SIBs, which could push forward the development of high energy and low cost energy storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqwFvgMEM3om7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj0aUOCMnZnNA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhs1ait7%252FE&amp;md5=2c6cca8c9d80a5d312f11af3558c8996</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.0c06296"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gong, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ahmed, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Battaglia, V.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Cagelike CoSe2@N-Doped Carbon Aerogels with Pseudocapacitive Properties as Advanced Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries with Excellent Rate Performance and Cyclic Stability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pan, Yuelei; Cheng, Xudong; Gao, Mengyao; Fu, Yanbao; Feng, Jun; Gong, Lunlun; Ahmed, Hoda; Zhang, Heping; Battaglia, Vincent S.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrochem. conversion reaction based electrodes offer a high sodium storage capacity in rechargeable batteries by utilizing the variable valence states of transition metals.  Thus, transition metal chalcogenides (TMCs) as such materials have been intensively investigated in recent years to explore the possibilities of practical application in rechargeable sodium-ion batteries; however, it is hindered by poor rate performance and a high-cost prepn. method.  In addn., some issues in regards to conversion reactions remain poorly understood, including incomplete reversible reaction processes, polarization, and hysteresis.  Herein, a novel cagelike CoSe2@N-doped carbon aerogels hybrid composite was designed and prepd. by a facile and high-efficiency sol-gel technol.  Benefiting from the surface engineering optimization, high charge transfer, and low-energy diffusion barrier, the CoSe2@N-doped carbon aerogels exhibit a high pseudocapacitive property.  Most importantly, the CoSe2 anode has been carefully investigated at different discharge/charge states by X-ray absorption near edge spectroscopy technologies and d. functional theory (DFT) simulations, which deeply reveal the capacity fading mechanism and phase transition behavior.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo1GpyrAwgv9bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj0aUOCMnZnNA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhtlSisL3I&amp;md5=0bf85dda690eb3e7bfcb35b959befaf3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1039/d1ta00226k"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Coupling Hierarchical Iron Cobalt Selenide Arrays with N-Doped Carbon as Advanced Anodes for Sodium Ion Storage</span>. <i>J. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>9</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">7248</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">7256</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Coupling hierarchical iron cobalt selenide arrays with N-doped carbon as advanced anodes for sodium ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Peijia; Huang, Jiajie; Zhang, Jing; Wang, Liang; Sun, Peiheng; Yang, Yefeng; Yao, Zhujun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7248-7256</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal selenides have emerged as a class of promising anodes for sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  However, the notorious issues of their low elec. cond. and huge vol. changes during sodium ion insertion/extn. lead to poor cycling stability and inferior rate capability.  In this work, hierarchically core-branched iron cobalt selenide arrays coated with N-doped carbon shell (denoted as FeCo-Se@NC) were rationally designed and synthesized on carbon cloth through a combined strategy of hydrothermal, selenization and carbonization processes.  Benefitting from the designed arrays with simultaneous Fe doping into the CoSe2 matrix and N-doped carbon coating, the optimized FeCo-Se@NC electrode possesses greatly enhanced structural integrity and accelerated ion/electron transfer kinetics.  When employed as a binder- and additive-free anode for SIBs, the FeCo-Se@NC electrode exhibits a high reversible capacity of 532.1 mA h g-1 at 0.05 A g-1, competitive rate capability (193.3 mA h g-1 at 5 A g-1), and good cycling stability (386.1 mA h g-1 after 150 cycles at 0.5 A g-1).  Moreover, when coupled with Na3V2(PO4)3/C, the full cell delivers a high capacity of 350.6 mA h g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 and a high energy d. of 276.7 W h kg-1.  This work is expected to provide a new avenue for the development of arrayed transition metal selenide-based materials for high-performance SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo2NuoajFW6OLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj0aUOCMnZnNA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXjs12jsrk%253D&amp;md5=3e55b0f8ee792deab0eccb34c859032a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1021/acssuschemeng.9b05474"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ke, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cong, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Deng, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Uniform Bi-Sb Alloy Nanoparticles Synthesized from MOFs by Laser Metallurgy for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Sustainable Chem.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Durian-Inspired Design of Bismuth-Antimony Alloy Arrays for Robust Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ni, Jiangfeng; Li, Xinyan; Sun, Menglei; Yuan, Yifei; Liu, Tongchao; Li, Liang; Lu, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">9117-9124</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries have attracted widespread attention for cost-effective and large-scale elec. energy storage.  However, their practical deployment has been largely retarded by the lack of choice of efficient anode materials featuring large capacity and electrochem. stability and robustness.  Herein, we report a durian-inspired design and template-free fabrication of a robust sodium anode based on triangular pyramid arrays of Bi0.75Sb0.25 alloy electrodeposited on Cu substrates.  The Bi0.75Sb0.25 arrays exhibit an appreciable electrochem. robustness for sodium storage, sustaining a reversible capability 335 mAh g-1 at a high rate of 2.5 A g-1 and 87% of the initial capacity over 2000 cycles.  We further demonstrate the applicability of the Bi0.75Sb0.25 array anode in sodium full cells by pairing it with a Na3V2(PO4)3/C cathode.  This full cell achieves a high specific energy of 203 Wh kg-1 (based on both active electrodes).  Such an enhanced performance is attributed to the thorny-durian-like architecture and bimetallic alloy compn.  The pyramid tip induces ion enrichment for rapid charge-transfer reaction, while the alloy design reduces the electrode vol. swelling for stable Na cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqLck-l7_HvOrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj0aUOCMnZnNA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXht1CltbzO&amp;md5=f310715ed1b7366e17639acccc30dd75</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1039/c9ta06273d"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tian, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, X.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hong, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Carbon-Coated CoSe<sub>2</sub> Nanoparticles Confined in N-Doped Carbon Microboxes with Enhanced Sodium Storage Properties</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon-coated CoSe2 nanoparticles confined in N-doped carbon microboxes with enhanced sodium storage properties</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tian, Jiawei; Li, Jia; Zhang, Yongxing; Yu, Xin-Yao; Hong, Zhanglian</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">37</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Due to their high theor. specific capacity, CoSe2-based anode materials have attracted enormous attention for sodium storage.  However, the poor cycling stability and rate capability still hinder their application.  Herein, starting from Co3[Co(CN)6]2 Prussian blue analog microcubes, a facile template-engaged strategy is developed to design and synthesize nanostructured dual-carbon-confined CoSe2 (denoted as DCC-CoSe2) microcubes.  In this unique nanostructure, N-doped carbon-coated CoSe2 nanoparticles are confined in N-doped carbon microboxes.  Benefiting from the desired structural features, the as-synthesized DCC-CoSe2 microcubes exhibit enhanced sodium storage properties in terms of high specific capacity (480 mA h g-1), excellent cycling stability (94.5% capacity retention over 2000 cycles), and superior rate capability (281 mA h g-1 at 20 A g-1).  The assembled full cell with DCC-CoSe2 microcubes as the anode material and Na3V2(PO4)3 as the cathode material can deliver a high initial capacity of 427 mA h g-1.  This work provides a new strategy for the rational design and synthesis of high performance metal selenide-based anode materials for sodium storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoIzc9GcmQHprVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljPZyBrswOZGQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhs1Ciu77P&amp;md5=176e20aeec2f2014510d53f22c2156ea</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1039/c8ta01168k"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Quasi-Reversible Conversion Reaction of CoSe<sub>2</sub>/Nitrogen-Doped Carbon Nanofibers Towards Long-Lifetime Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Quasi-reversible conversion reaction of CoSe2/nitrogen-doped carbon nanofibers towards long-lifetime anode materials for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cui, Chao; Wei, Zengxi; Zhou, Gang; Wei, Weifeng; Ma, Jianmin; Chen, Libao; Li, Chengchao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">16</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Developing electrode materials with a full conversion reaction is an effective route to break through the capacity barriers, but this goal remains a great challenge.  In this work, we report the synthesis of CoSe2 anodes with a quasi-reversible conversion reaction by uniformly encapsulating CoSe2 nanoparticles in nitrogen-doped carbon nanofibers (CoSe2/N-CNFs).  The space-confined effect of CNFs effectively inhibits pulverization and amorphization of CoSe2 during charge and discharge and thus remarkably ensures the integrity of the crystal structure.  Meanwhile, pseudocapacitive contributed by the size effect of CoSe2 nanodots and excellent cond. due to doped nitrogen heteroatoms give the electrode outstanding electrochem. properties.  When used as an anode, the CoSe2/N-CNFs achieved a reversible capacity of 371.8 mA h g-1 after 500 cycles at 0.2 A g-1.  Even at a high c.d. of 2 A g-1, the discharge capacity of the CoSe2/N-CNFs still reached 308 mA h g-1 after 1000 cycles with excellent rate performance.  The first principles calcns. demonstrate that the heterointerfaces between CoSe2 and nitrogen-doped carbon can significantly enhance the stability of the structure and improve the storage/diffusion capability of Na+.  Moreover, ex situ high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy (HRTEM) and selected area electron diffraction (SAED) reveal that the unique structure enables quasi-reversible cryst.-phase transformation of CoSe2, which leads to the superior cycling stability of the battery with high capacity retention.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGohwL1EoQIXL7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljPZyBrswOZGQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Exploration of fast ion diffusion kinetics in graphene nanoscrolls encapsulated CoSe2 as advanced anode for high-rate sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Zhigang; Lin, Jun; Hao, Junyang; Xue, Fangfang; Gu, Yuefeng; Zhu, Zhicheng; Li, Qiuhong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have drawn much attention due to the abundance and low cost of sodium.  However, electrode materials of SIBs displayed sluggish Na+ diffusivity and fatal vol. expansion, owing to the larger ionic radius of Na+ ions than Li+ ions.  In this work, we built the CoSe2 nanoparticles embedded in graphene nanoscrolls (GNS) as advanced anodes for high-rate SIBs.  The CoSe2/C@GNS anodes exhibited a high reversible capacity of 545 mA h g-1 at 0.2 A g-1. The CoSe2/C@GNS anode also demonstrate ultrahigh rate capabilities (212.5 mAh g-1 at 50 A g-1).  In addn., with a high mass loading (6 mg cm-2), the electrode still displayed a stable capacity (412 mA h g-1 1 A g-1).  The fast electron transfer and Na+ ion diffusion kinetics creates the excellent electrochem. properties, on account of the uniform arrangement of nanoparticles and unique reticular crosslinking structure of CoSe2/C@GNS.  This strategy could also be constructed other electrode materials, which provides more probabilities for the development of SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoarOMWJXXoM7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljPZyBrswOZGQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhtFCmtr3M&amp;md5=0410f336c00fce41d4d2ff3228dbe115</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2019.12.060"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jing, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Encapsulating Yolk-Shell FeS<sub>2</sub>@Carbon Microboxes into Interconnected Graphene Framework for Ultrafast Lithium/Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Carbon</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>159</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">366</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">377</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Encapsulating yolk-shell FeS2@carbon microboxes into interconnected graphene framework for ultrafast lithium/sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jing, Peng; Wang, Qiong; Wang, Boya; Gao, Xu; Zhang, Yun; Wu, Hao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pyrite FeS2 has been accepted as one promising anode candidate for lithium- (LIBs) and sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to its extremely high theor. capacity of 894 mAh g-1.  However, the practical capabilities including rate performance and cycling stability of FeS2-based materials are still restricted by exaggerated vol. variation and sluggish ions kinetics.  Herein, an interesting dual-carbon decorated strategy is upgraded to address these issues.  The resultant material features a hierarchical architecture with yolk-shell FeS2@carbon microboxes as well as interconnected graphene framework (GF/FeS2@C).  By virtue of the dual-carbon protection effect and binary channel for electrons/ions transfer, the GF/FeS2@C composites exhibit superior Li and Na storage performance.  For LIBs, it shows superior rate capability of 428 mAh g-1 at 20 A g-1 and decent long-term cycle stability.  As for SIBs, it delivers a reversible capacity of 200 mAh g-1 at high c.d. of 10 A g-1 and ultra-long lifespan at 0.5 A g-1 (257 mAh g-1 after 1000 cycles) and 2 A g-1 (203 mAh g-1 after 600 cycles).         (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">370</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Currently, a great challenge to the design of durable sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) is the need for the architecture of nanostructured transition metal-selenide electrodes with high capacity and excellent cycling stability.  In this paper, a novel metal-org. framework (MOF)-induced approach is described to construct necklace-like carbon nanotube (CNT)-CoSe2@N-doped carbon (NC) with excellent sodium ion storage performance.  In this strategy, CNT-threaded zeolitic imidazolate framework-67 (ZIF-67) polyhedra, synthesized by wet chem. methods, are used as the precursor.  During the selenization step, ZIF-67 polyhedra transform into mesoporous nanoclusters consisted of CoSe2@NC nanoparticles, forming CNT-CoSe2@NC composites with a necklace-like morphol.  Such structures facilitate ion and electron transport, and inhibit the aggregation and pulverization of active materials during cycling processes via the intimate contact between the CNTs and CoSe2@NC.  The as-designed composites show significantly improved electrochem. properties including high discharge capacity (404 mA·h·g-1 after 120 cycles at 0.2 A·g-1), excellent rate performance (363 mA·h·g-1 at 5.0 A·g-1), and reasonable capacity retention (80% when calcd. from the 2nd cycle).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqpMO4IcaEX4rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljPZyBrswOZGQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXms1Gmu74%253D&amp;md5=1b833c6983582fdf01086e175b596052</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2017.07.079"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, S.-K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Excellent sodium-ion storage performances of CoSe2 nanoparticles embedded within N-doped porous graphitic carbon nanocube/carbon nanotube composite</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Park, Seung-Keun; Kim, Jin Koo; Kang, Yun Chan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A metal org. framework (MOF)-engaged approach is applied for the fabrication of CoSe2 nanoparticles embedded within N-doped porous graphitic C nanocubes/C nanotubes (CoSe2@N-PGC/CNTs).  The composites were prepd. by decompn. under the reducing atm. and further selenization of Co-based zeolitic imidazolate framework (ZIF-67) precursor.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synthesis of Nitrogen-Doped Mesoporous Structures from Metal-Organic Frameworks and Their Utilization Enabling High Performances in Hybrid Sodium-Ion Energy Storages</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lee, Gyu Heon; Kang, Jeung Ku</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Science (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion energy storage is of the most attractive candidate for commercialization adoption due to the safety and cost demands of large-scale energy storage systems, but its low energy d., slow charging capability, and poor cycle stability are yet to be overcome.  Here, a strategy is reported to realize high-performance sodium-ion energy storage using battery-type anode and capacitor-type cathode materials.  First, nitrogen-doped mesoporous titanium dioxide (NMTiO2) structures are synthesized via the controlled pyrolysis of metal-org. frameworks.  They exhibit interconnected open mesopores allowing fast ion transport and robust cycle stability with nearly 100% coulombic efficiency, along with rich redox-reactive sites allowing high capacity even at a high rate of ≈90 C. Moreover, assembling the NMTiO2 anode with the nitrogen-doped graphene (NG) cathode in an asym. full cell shows a high energy d. exceeding its counterpart sym. cell by more than threefold as well as robust cycle stability over 10 000 cycles.  Addnl., it gives a high-power d. close to 26 000 W kg-1 outperforming that of a conventional sodium-ion battery by several hundred fold, so that full cells can be charged within a few tens of seconds by the flexible photovoltaic charging and universal serial bus charging modules.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpjlMspdR5xcrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljkD55CmwNrpQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXntl2rtb8%253D&amp;md5=0a7e3f7013c7fd997b7aa415eb688a6e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1016/j.jallcom.2020.158190"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hong, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ren, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sulfur and Nitrogen-Doped Li<sub>4</sub>Ti<sub>5</sub>O<sub>12</sub>/RGO as an Anode Material for Advanced Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sulfur and nitrogen-doped Li4Ti5O12/rGO as an anode material for advanced sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liang, Kang; Huang, Xiaobing; Hong, Xianda; Liao, Yuanhong; Ren, Yurong; Wang, Haiyan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Alloys and Compounds</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">857</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Finding a high-performance anode material is still a large challenge for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) since two com. anode materials in lithium-ion batteries, graphite, and silicon exhibit very poor sodium storage performance.  Li4Ti5O12 (LTO) has become a promising candidate for SIBs mainly due to its robust structural stability.  However, the utilization of LTO in SIBs was greatly limited due to its inferior cond. and ion diffusion coeff.  To solve the above problems, in this work, structural regulating and surface modification were employed simultaneously to fabricate sulfur and nitrogen-doped LTO/reduced graphene oxide (SN-LTO/rGO) through the hydrothermal method following the calcination process with thiourea.  Because of the synergistic effect of the rGO network and SN-doping, the as-obtained SN-LTO/rGO sample boasts a high discharge capacity of 132.5 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 when applied as an anode in SIBs.  It is pointed out that under the c.d. of 500 mA g-1, the discharge capacity still kept 84.6 mAh g-1 after 500 cycles, and the capacity remains at 87.40% of the initial value, indicating excellent rate performance and cycle stability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr3spIeRr94ZrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljkD55CmwNrpQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">TiO2-Coated Interlayer-Expanded MoSe2/Phosphorus-Doped Carbon Nanospheres for Ultrafast and Ultralong Cycling Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang Yuyu; Kang Wenpei; Cao Dongwei; Li Chenxu; Cao Dongxu; Kang Zixi; Sun Daofeng; Wang Rongming; Wang Yunxiao; Cao Yuliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced science (Weinheim, Baden-Wurttemberg, Germany)</span>

                        cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultralong life lithium-ion battery anode with superior high-rate capability and excellent cyclic stability from mesoporous Fe2O3@TiO2 core-shell nanorods</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Xiao; Chen, Haoxin; Xie, Yaping; Guo, Jinxue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Mesoporous core-shell nanocomposites with porous α-Fe2O3 nanorods as the core and porous TiO2 as the shell are synthesized by calcination treatment of FeOOH@TiO2 core-shell nanorods.  Due to the high capacity of Fe2O3 core and durable outer shell of TiO2, as well as the specific mesoporous nanostructures, the products deliver an excellent electrochem. performance towards lithium storage, including stable reversible capacity as high as ∼860 mA-h/g at high c.d. of 1 A/g, excellent cyclic stability with ultralong cycling life over 1000 cycles, and outstanding rate capability.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">TiO2 as a multifunction coating layer to enhance the electrochemical performance of SiOx@TiO2@C composite as anode material</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiao, Zhexi; Yu, Chunhui; Lin, Xianqing; Chen, Xiao; Zhang, Chenxi; Jiang, Hairong; Zhang, Rufan; Wei, Fei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">77</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">SiOx-based anode materials suffer from inherent defects of vol. expansion, high initial capacity loss, and the huge electron and ion resistance in the unstable solid electrolyte interphase layer impede their commercialization.  Surface coating is the most prevalent strategy for resolving the key concerns.  In this paper, we present a dual-shell coating structural composite (denoted as SiOx@TiO2@C) through a two-step process.  By introducing a high-quality anatase-phase TiO2 layer, a highly stable interface and decreased resistance to electron and ion diffusion of composite are achieved and investigated systematically.  Addnl., the side reactivity is studied firstly.  Moreover, the enhanced safety of the electrode is evaluated.  The as-prepd. composite exhibites a high initial discharge capacity of 1624.7 mAh g-1 with an initial coulombic efficiency (ICE) of 81.2%, capacity retention of 89.5% (vs 2nd discharge) after 800 cycles, and a reversible capacity of 949.7 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1.  The assembled full-cell exhibites an initial area capacity of 2.6 mAh cm-2 with an ICE higher than 90%; the exceeding 106 times and 60 times increase in electron cond. and Li+ cond. facilitate electron and ion diffusion particularly at high rates.  The probable reasons assocd. with the interface stability are discussed and proposed in this paper.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrTIryvZ_6_brVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljkD55CmwNrpQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhsVCls7%252FK&amp;md5=b73f7886e8c9f58a3a2935eb86f121d7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2020.126873"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Multi-Role TiO<sub>2</sub> Layer Coated Carbon@Few-Layered MoS<sub>2</sub> Nanotubes for Durable Lithium Storage</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Multi-role TiO2 layer coated carbon@few-layered MoS2 nanotubes for durable lithium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Junfeng; Han, Lu; Zhang, Xinlu; Sun, Hengchao; Liu, Xinjuan; Lu, Ting; Yao, Yefeng; Pan, Likun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">406</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The combination of transitional-metal dichalcogenides with rigid TiO2 has been proved to be an effective strategy to improve their structural stability but the poor long-term cycling stability at high c.d. still hinders their practical applications.  In this paper, a smart structure consisting of multi-role TiO2 coated on carbon@few-layered MoS2 (CMT) nanotubes was synthesized to achieve superior long-term cycling performance.  In this unique structure, the anatase/rutile TiO2 is explored as a coating layer of MoS2, which not only accommodates the vol. change resulting from the phase transformation from S to Li2S but also alleviates the ''shuttle effect'' caused by the dissoln. of long-chain lithium polysulfides.  Moreover, the carbon nanotubes serve as a conductive backbone for MoS2 to improve the electron transport ability of electrode and the few-layered MoS2 nanosheets with expanded interlayers can shorten the lithium-ion pathway and improve the lithium-ion diffusion mobility.  Benefitting from the synergetic effects of TiO2 layer, carbon and MoS2, when applied as anode of LIBs, the CMT demonstrates an extraordinary long-term cycling performance (528.5 mAh g-1 at 1000 mA g-1 and 455.2 mAh g-1 at 2000 mA g-1 after 1000 cycles), which outperforms most of the MoS2-TiO2 based anode materials reported before.  This work should offer new perspectives into exploring high-performance MoS2-TiO2 based anode materials for efficient lithium storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGro2-RO2wwLFbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgcN6Nt-tV4gA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhslyntL7J&amp;md5=c7d62f1de888172d7f05340a882d2fbf</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemrev.0c00170"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fleischmann, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mitchell, J.                         cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pseudocapacitance: From Fundamental Understanding to High Power Energy Storage Materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Fleischmann, Simon; Mitchell, James B.; Wang, Ruocun; Zhan, Cheng; Jiang, De-en; Presser, Volker; Augustyn, Veronica</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Reviews (Washington, DC, United States)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">120</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">14</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6738-6782</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CHREAY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0009-2665</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  There is an urgent global need for electrochem. energy storage that includes materials that can provide simultaneous high power and high energy d.  One strategy to achieve this goal is with pseudocapacitive materials that take advantage of reversible surface or near-surface Faradaic reactions to store charge.  This allows them to surpass the capacity limitations of elec. double-layer capacitors and the mass transfer limitations of batteries.  The past decade has seen tremendous growth in the understanding of pseudocapacitance as well as materials that exhibit this phenomenon.  The purpose of this Review is to examine the fundamental development of the concept of pseudocapacitance and how it came to prominence in electrochem. energy storage as well as to describe new classes of materials whose electrochem. energy storage behavior can be described as pseudocapacitive.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrwJEuYlBvPxrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgcN6Nt-tV4gA"> &gt;&gt; return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1007/s40820-020-00567-2"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Peng, D.-L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High-Energy and High-Power Pseudocapacitor-Battery Hybrid Sodium-Ion Capacitor with Na(+) Intercalation Pseudocapacitance Anode</span>. <i>Nano-Micro Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>13</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">55</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1007/s40820-020-00567-2</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D13%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D55%26journal%3DNano-Micro%2BLett.%26author%3DQ.%2BWei%26author%3DQ.%2BLi%26author%3DY.%2BJiang%26author%3DY.%2BZhao%26author%3DS.%2BTan%26author%3DJ.%2BDong%26author%3DL.%2BMai%26author%3DD.-L.%2BPeng%26title%3DHigh-Energy%2Band%2BHigh-Power%2BPseudocapacitor-Battery%2BHybrid%2BSodium-Ion%2BCapacitor%2Bwith%2BNa%2528%252B%2529%2BIntercalation%2BPseudocapacitance%2BAnode%26doi%3D10.1007%252Fs40820-020-00567-2&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c20154&amp;doiOfLink=10.1007%2Fs40820-020-00567-2&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-Energy and High-Power Pseudocapacitor-Battery Hybrid Sodium-Ion Capacitor with Na(+) Intercalation Pseudocapacitance Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wei Qiulong; Peng Dong-Liang; Li Qidong; Jiang Yalong; Tan Shuangshuang; Dong Jun; Mai Liqiang; Zhao Yunlong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano-micro letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">55</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">High-performance and low-cost sodium-ion capacitors (SICs) show tremendous potential applications in public transport and grid energy storage.  However, conventional SICs are limited by the low specific capacity, poor rate capability, and low initial coulombic efficiency (ICE) of anode materials.  Herein, we report layered iron vanadate (Fe5V15O39 (OH)9·9H2O) ultrathin nanosheets with a thickness of ~ 2.2 nm (FeVO UNSs) as a novel anode for rapid and reversible sodium-ion storage.  According to in situ synchrotron X-ray diffractions and electrochemical analysis, the storage mechanism of FeVO UNSs anode is Na(+) intercalation pseudocapacitance under a safe potential window.  The FeVO UNSs anode delivers high ICE (93.86%), high reversible capacity (292 mAh g(-1)), excellent cycling stability, and remarkable rate capability.  Furthermore, a pseudocapacitor-battery hybrid SIC (PBH-SIC) consisting of pseudocapacitor-type FeVO UNSs anode and battery-type Na3(VO)2(PO4)2F cathode is assembled with the elimination of presodiation treatments.  The PBH-SIC involves faradaic reaction on both cathode and anode materials, delivering a high energy density of 126 Wh kg(-1) at 91 W kg(-1), a high power density of 7.6 kW kg(-1) with an energy density of 43 Wh kg(-1), and 9000 stable cycles.  The tunable vanadate materials with high-performance Na(+) intercalation pseudocapacitance provide a direction for developing next-generation high-energy capacitors.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcSNIXzBS4qhe7YtC3U5jeOifW6udTcc2eYu9mmdgeHLNbntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BB2c7pt1OjtA%253D%253D&amp;md5=a9032e5b0b643ed75a263db06574a681</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1039/c7ta08538a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hierarchical Nanotubes Constructed from Interlayer-Expanded MoSe<sub>2</sub> Nanosheets as a Highly Durable Electrode for Sodium Storage</span>. <i>J.
