                        cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical nanotubes constructed from interlayer-expanded MoSe2 nanosheets as a highly durable electrode for sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Junjun; Wu, Meihui; Liu, Tong; Kang, Wenpei; Xu, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">47</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">24859-24866</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as a promising energy storage device, but suffer from poor cycling performance.  Here, hierarchical MoSe2 nanotubes were synthesized for the 1st time and demonstrated as a highly durable electrode material of SIBs.  The hierarchical nanotubes consist of few-layered MoSe2 nanosheets with an expanded (002) interlayer spacing of 1.00 nm (54.8% expansion).  The growth of hierarchical nanotubes is a result of oriented attachment and Ostwald ripening effects.  As a robust Na host material, the MoSe2 nanotubes featuring hierarchical organization, hollow interiors, and interlayer expansion are beneficial for (1) lowering diffusion energy barriers and facilitating fast Na+ insertion/extn. reaction kinetics, (2) accommodating vol. changes upon sodiation/desodiation, (3) preserving structural and morphol. stability, and (4) improving electronic cond. by in situ C modification.  By controlling the cut-off voltage of 0.5-3.0 V with an intercalation mechanism, the MoSe2 nanotube electrode shows highly stable cycling performance and delivers a reversible discharge capacity of 228 mAh/g after 1500 cycles at a high c.d. of 1000 mA/g.  This work demonstrates the best cycling performance to date of MoSe2-based anodes for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoj6cQOT7qzKLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgcN6Nt-tV4gA"> &gt;&gt;                 10.1021/acsnano.9b05614</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D13%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D10787-10797%26journal%3DACS%2BNano%26author%3DY.%2BJiang%26author%3DG.%2BZou%26author%3DH.%2BHou%26author%3DJ.%2BLi%26author%3DC.%2BLiu%26author%3DX.%2BQiu%26author%3DX.%2BJi%26title%3DComposition%2BEngineering%2BBoosts%2BVoltage%2BWindows%2Bfor%2BAdvanced%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsnano.9b05614&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c20154&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsnano.9b05614&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Composition Engineering Boosts Voltage Windows for Advanced Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jiang, Yunling; Zou, Guoqiang; Hou, Hongshuai; Li, Jiayang; Liu, Cheng; Qiu, Xiaoqing; Ji, Xiaobo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">10787-10797</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition-metal selenides have captured sustainable research attention in energy storage and conversion field as promising anodes for sodium-ion batteries.  However, for the majority of transition metal selenides, the potential windows have to compress to 0.5-3.0 V for the maintenance of cycling and rate capability, which largely sacrifices the capacity under low voltage and impair energy d. for sodium full batteries.  Herein, through introducing diverse metal ions, transition-metal selenides consisted of different compn. doping (CoM-Se2@NC, M = Ni, Cu, Zn) are prepd. with more stable structures and higher cond., which exhibit superior cycling and rate properties than those of CoSe2@NC even at a wider voltage range for sodium ion batteries.  In particular, Zn2+ doping demonstrates the most prominent sodium storage performance among series materials, delivering a high capacity of 474 mAh g-1 after 80 cycles at 500 mA g-1 and rate capacities of 511.4, 382.7, 372.1, 339.2, 306.8, and 291.4 mAh g-1 at current densities of 0.1, 0.5, 1.0, 1.4, 1.8, and 2.0 A g-1, resp.  The compn. adjusting strategy based on metal ions doping can optimize electrochem. performances of metal selenides, offer an avenue to expand stable voltage windows, and provide a feasible approach for the construction of high specific energy sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqdgjjIFBgG4bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgcN6Nt-tV4gA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Defect-assisted selective surface phosphorus doping to enhance rate capability of titanium dioxide for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Gan, Qingmeng; He, Hanna; Zhu, Youhuan; Wang, Zhenyu; Qin, Ning; Gu, Shuai; Li, Zhiqiang; Luo, Wen; Lu, Zhouguang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">9247-9258</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Phosphorus doping is an effective strategy to simultaneously improve the electronic cond. and regulate the ionic diffusion kinetics of TiO2 being considered as anode materials for sodium ion batteries.  However, efficient phosphorus doping at high concn. in well-crystd. TiO2 nanoparticles is still a big challenge.  Herein, the authors propose a defect-assisted phosphorus doping strategy to selectively engineer the surface structure of TiO2 nanoparticles.  The reduced TiO2-x shell layer that is rich in oxygen defects and Ti3+ species precisely triggered a high concn. of phosphorus doping (∼7.8 at.%), and consequently a TiO2@TiO2-x-P core@shell architecture was produced.  Comprehensive characterizations and first-principle calcns. proved that the surface-functionalized TiO2-x-P thin layer endowed the TiO2@TiO2-x-P with substantially enhanced electronic cond. and accelerated Na ion transportation, resulting in great rate capability (167 mA h g-1 at 10 000 mA g-1) and stable cycling (99% after 5000 cycles at 10 A g-1).  Combining in/ex situ x-ray diffraction with ex situ ESR clearly demonstrated the high reversibility and robust mech. behavior of TiO2@TiO2-x-P upon long-term cycling.  This work provides an interesting and effective strategy for precise heteroatoms doping to improve the electrochem. performance of nanoparticles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoV2X3aWTMl9bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgfgKguVhzRqA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhsVamtb7P&amp;md5=cd8e232f3259e7881601dbcf23b2e6ee</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref47'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit47" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202002019"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, H.                         cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Interface-Induced Pseudocapacitance in Nonporous Heterogeneous Particles for High Volumetric Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Bo; Liu, Qianqian; Chen, Yujie; Liu, Qian; Yu, Qian; Wu, Hao Bin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">30</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Developing pseudocapacitive materials for electrochem. energy storage generally relies on the formation of nanosize and/or nanoporous particles with short solid-state diffusion distance and high surface area, which leads to low volumetric capacity and severe parasitic reactions.  In this work, nonporous bulky heterogeneous particles composed of TiO2 matrix and phosphorus are reported for high volumetric pseudocapacitive Na storage.  An in situ formed 3D titanium phosphate interphase serves as a fast ionic transport network, allowing rapid sodiation/desodiation processes within the particles.  Such nonporous heterogeneous particles exhibit "interface-induced pseudocapacitance" with an enhanced volumetric capacity, which is over 50% higher than that of com. hard carbon anodes.  This study demonstrates heterogeneous particles with a well-engineered nanostructure as a new paradigm for electrode materials design.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrDyL1REGY6qbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgfgKguVhzRqA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhs1ertLfK&amp;md5=821619f29b79e396307ef153d92c3a64</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref48'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.8b01888"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ge, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Three-Dimensional Hierarchical Framework Assembled by Cobblestone-Like CoSe<sub>2</sub>@C Nanospheres for Ultrastable Sodium-Ion Storage</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                         cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Three-Dimensional Hierarchical Framework Assembled by Cobblestone-Like CoSe2@C Nanospheres for Ultrastable Sodium-Ion Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ge, Peng; Hou, Hongshuai; Li, Sijie; Huang, Lanping; Ji, Xiaobo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), as the promising com. energy system, are restricted by their sluggish kinetics and low sodium-ion storage.  Metal selenide possesses good cond. and capacity but still suffers from the stacked problem and vol. expansion.  Significantly, CoSe2/C is successfully prepd. with the assistance of citric acid as both a chelating agent and carbon precursor, displaying that cobblestone-like nanospheres with the radii (&lt;25 nm) distribute uniformly in the carbon matrix.  It is expected that the established Co-O-C bonds enhance the stability of the structure with faster ion shuttling.  With the available electrolyte (NaCF3SO3/diethylene glycol di-Me ether) in a potential window range from 0.5 to 3.0 V, the as-obtained sample shows the ultralong lifespan at 4.5 A g-1, retaining a capacity of 345 mA h g-1 after 10 000 cycles.  From the detailed kinetic anal., it is clear that the surface-controlled electrochem. behavior mainly contributes to the excellent large-current cycling stability and Na storage capacity.  The ex situ results support that the crystal and morphol. structure remains stable.  This work is anticipated to enhance the in-depth understanding of the CoSe2/C anode and supply a facile manner to obtain electrode materials for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqFiCoFI7FUHLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgfgKguVhzRqA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXnsValsbs%253D&amp;md5=4c9419da63d1fcfd3d5a736c7d1bd207</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref49'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit49" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202003391"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jo, M.                         cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Golden Bristlegrass-Like Hierarchical Graphene Nanofibers Entangled with N-Doped CNTs Containing CoSe2 Nanocrystals at Each Node as Anodes for High-Rate Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jo, Min Su; Lee, Jae Seob; Jeong, Sun Young; Kim, Jae Kwang; Kang, Yun Chan; Kang, Dong Won; Jeong, Sang Mun; Cho, Jung Sang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Golden bristlegrass-like unique nanostructures comprising reduced graphene oxide (rGO) matrixed nanofibers entangled with bamboo-like N-doped carbon nanotubes (CNTs) contg. CoSe2 nanocrystals at each node (denoted as N-CNT/rGO/CoSe2 NF) are designed as anodes for high-rate sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Bamboo-like N-doped CNTs (N-CNTs) are successfully generated on the rGO matrixed nanofiber surface, between rGO sheets and mesopores, and interconnected chem. with homogeneously distributed rGO sheets.  The defects in the N-CNTs formed by a simple etching process allow the complete phase conversion of Co into CoSe2 through the efficient penetration of H2Se gas inside the CNT walls.  The N-CNTs bridge the vertical defects for electron transfer in the rGO sheet layers and increase the distance between the rGO sheets during cycles.  The discharge capacity of N-CNT/rGO/CoSe2 NF after the 10 000th cycle at an extremely high c.d. of 10 A g-1 is 264 mA h g-1, and the capacity retention measured at the 100th cycle is 89%.  N-CNT/rGO/CoSe2 NF has final discharge capacities of 395, 363, 328, 304, 283, 263, 246, 223, 197, 171, and 151 mA h g-1 at current densities of 1, 2, 4, 6, 8, 10, 12, 14, 16, 18, and 20 A g-1, resp.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpkHbBe0K-jKrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgfgKguVhzRqA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhs1Kksr3P&amp;md5=6f750465429ff005826b72c15206183f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref50'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit50" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2020.127400"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrospinning Fabrication of Flexible, Foldable, and Twistable Sb<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>/C Nanofiber Anode for Lithium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem. Eng. J.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>413</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">127400</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.cej.2020.127400</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D413%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D127400%26journal%3DChem.%2BEng.%2BJ.%26author%3DJ.%2BXia%26author%3DX.%2BZhang%26author%3DY.%2BYang%26author%3DX.%2BWang%26author%3DJ.%2BYao%26title%3DElectrospinning%2BFabrication%2Bof%2BFlexible%252C%2BFoldable%252C%2Band%2BTwistable%2BSb2S3%252FTiO2%252FC%2BNanofiber%2BAnode%2Bfor%2BLithium%2BIon%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.cej.2020.127400&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c20154&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.cej.2020.127400&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrospinning fabrication of flexible, foldable, and twistable Sb2S3/TiO2/C nanofiber anode for lithium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xia, Jing; Zhang, Xin; Yang, Yongan; Wang, Xi; Yao, Jiannian</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">413</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">127400</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMEJAJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1385-8947</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Flexible batteries are one of the key components of flexible electronic devices.  To develop flexible batteries with excellent mech. durability and electrochem. performance, electrode design is the crit. part.  Electrospinning technol. is a popular strategy for producing flexible electrodes.  However, the nanofiber membranes prepd. by traditional electrospinning methods without additives have poor mech. flexibility due to the collapse of the fiber structure during heat treatment caused by the incompatibility and low adhesion of the interface between the polymer and transition metal ions.  Herein, we propose a method of using titanium (IV) isopropoxide as coupling agent to enhance the thermotolerant and mech. properties of nanofibers.  The porous Sb2S3/TiO2/C nanofiber membrane is prepd. by adding an appropriate amt. of titanium (IV) isopropoxide as the coupling agent.  The prepd. nanofiber membranes remain intact and crease-free after 4-folded manipulation.  The porous Sb2S3/TiO2/C nanofiber membranes are cut into electrodes and directly assembled into lithium-ion half-cells or full-cells without slurry coating processes.  In lithium-ion half-cells, the porous Sb2S3/TiO2/C nanofiber membranes could cycle 800 times at a c.d. of 2000 mA g-1.  In lithium-ion full-cells, a high discharge capacity of 261.6 mAh g-1 can obtained after 100 cycles when cycled at 50 mA g-1.  More importantly, the fully charged full-cell can turn on 16 red light-emitting diodes, demonstrating the practical utility of the porous Sb2S3/TiO2/C nanofiber membrane in flexible lithium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrEYwNAeJ5vDLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgfgKguVhzRqA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXit1GjsL7I&amp;md5=088357f817882eecf85e47375f8cc0ce</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2019.01.062"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qu, H.-Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, R.-Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, M.-Q.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Long Cycle Life and High Rate Capability of Three Dimensional CoSe<sub>2</sub> Grain-Attached Carbon Nanofibers for Flexible Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>58</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">715</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">723</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Long cycle life and high rate capability of three dimensional CoSe2 grain-attached carbon nanofibers for flexible sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yin, Hong; Qu, Hong-Qing; Liu, Zhitian; Jiang, Ren-Zhi; Li, Chong; Zhu, Ming-Qiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">58</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">715-723</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The flexible binderless films composed of cobalt selenide grains attached on carbon nanofibers (denoted as CoSe2/CNFs) are prepd. by electrospinning to enhance the electronic cond., Na-ions diffusion and alleviate vol. variation during charge/discharge process for high performance sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  The binderless and flexible CoSe2/CNFs electrode can obtain a high reversible capacity of 430 mAh g-1 after 400 cycles at a c.d. of 200 mA g-1, an exceptional rate capability of 224 mAh g-1 at 15 A g-1, even a capacity of 370 mAh g-1 at 2 A g-1 after 1000 cycles.  The superior electrochem. performance can be ascribed to the synergistic effects of the homogeneous distribution of CoSe2 grains attached to the carbon nanofibers and the high electronic cond. framework of 3D interconnecting carbon nanofibers, which can alleviate the vol. variation during charge-discharge process and sustain the high elec. cond. and fast Na-ions diffusion throughout the electrode.  This binderless flexible CoSe2/CNFs nanocomposite electrode may hold great application promising for high cycling performance SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqNFZc8d6Oju7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhewmrlm55lWA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXivFylsb8%253D&amp;md5=4bce2f90d419d74bced0c3dbd48c45bf</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref52'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">52</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit52" data-doi="10.1016/j.mtener.2020.100631"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Doping-Induced Polymorph Transformation to Boost Ultrafast Sodium Storage in Hierarchical CoSe<sub>2</sub>-Carbon Arrays</span>. <i>Mater. Today Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>20</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">100631</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.mtener.2020.100631</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D20%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D100631%26journal%3DMater.%2BToday%2BEnergy%26author%3DW.%2BLi%26author%3DZ.%2BLiu%26author%3DH.%2BYang%26author%3DZ.%2BWang%26author%3DZ.%2BChen%26author%3DP.%2BLiang%26author%3DJ.%2BWang%26author%3DX.%2BShen%26title%3DDoping-Induced%2BPolymorph%2BTransformation%2Bto%2BBoost%2BUltrafast%2BSodium%2BStorage%2Bin%2BHierarchical%2BCoSe2-Carbon%2BArrays%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.mtener.2020.100631&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c20154&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.mtener.2020.100631&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Doping-induced polymorph transformation to boost ultrafast sodium storage in hierarchical CoSe2-carbon arrays</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, W.; Liu, Z.; Yang, H.; Wang, Z.; Chen, Z.; Liang, P.; Wang, J.; Shen, X.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Today Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">20</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">100631</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">MTEACH</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2468-6069</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal dichalcogenides (TMDs) are regarded as the most potential candidates of anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) owing to their high theor. capacity, while the sluggish kinetics and huge vol. variation that are accompanied by sodium-ion insertion/extn. cause inferior electrochem. performance.  Herein, a P-doping-induced polymorph transformation strategy is proposed to modulate the electronic structure of CoSe2 anode toward fast sodium storage.  D. functional theory (DFT) calcns. verify the unique effect of doping-induced polymorph engineering on modulating the electronic structure of CoSe2.  Therefore, due to the optimal electronic structure, improved ionic diffusion kinetics, and numerous exposure of reactive sites from hierarchical arrays, the P-CoSe2/NC anode exhibits impressive rate capability (459 mA h g-1 at 2 A g-1) when used as an anode for SIBs.  Our doping-induced polymorph engineering may be applicable to other advanced electrodes toward energy storage applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGok1hJLjGcZybVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhewmrlm55lWA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXls1Sht70%253D&amp;md5=579d9c4302445644bf8829e01c872c2a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref53"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref53'); <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lei, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Metal Organic Framework-Templated Synthesis of Bimetallic Selenides with Rich Phase Boundaries for Sodium-Ion Storage and Oxygen Evolution Reaction</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>13</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">5635</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">5645</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsnano.9b00816</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D13%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D5635-5645%26journal%3DACS%2BNano%26author%3DG.%2BFang%26author%3DQ.%2BWang%26author%3DJ.%2BZhou%26author%3DY.%2BLei%26author%3DZ.%2BChen%26author%3DZ.%2BWang%26author%3DA.%2BPan%26author%3DS.%2BLiang%26title%3DMetal%2BOrganic%2BFramework-Templated%2BSynthesis%2Bof%2BBimetallic%2BSelenides%2Bwith%2BRich%2BPhase%2BBoundaries%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BStorage%2Band%2BOxygen%2BEvolution%2BReaction%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsnano.9b00816&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c20154&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsnano.9b00816&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit53R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">53</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Metal Organic Framework-Templated Synthesis of Bimetallic Selenides with Rich Phase Boundaries for Sodium-Ion Storage and Oxygen Evolution Reaction</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Fang, Guozhao; Wang, Qichen; Zhou, Jiang; Lei, Yongpeng; Chen, Zixian; Wang, Ziqing; Pan, Anqiang; Liang, Shuquan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5635-5645</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Two-phase or multiphase compds. have been evidenced to exhibit good electrochem. performance for energy applications; however, the mechanism insights into these materials, esp. the performance improvement by engineering the high-active phase boundaries in bimetallic compds., remain to be seen.  Here, we report a bimetallic selenide heterostructure (CoSe2/ZnSe) and the fundamental mechanism behind their superior electrochem. performance.  The charge redistribution at the phase boundaries of CoSe2/ZnSe was exptl. and theor. proven.  Benefiting from the abundant phase boundaries, CoSe2/ZnSe exerts low Na+ adsorption energy and fast diffusion kinetics for sodium-ion batteries and high activity for oxygen evolution reaction.  As expected, excellent sodium storage capability, specifically a superb cyclic stability of up to 800 cycles for the Na3V2(PO4)3‖CoZn-Se full cell, and efficient water oxidn. with a small overpotential of 320 mV to reach 10 mA cm-2 were obtained.  This work demonstrates the importance of phase boundaries in bimetallic compds. to boost the performance in various fields.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp6OnaY1z2AW7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhewmrlm55lWA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXot1yjt78%253D&amp;md5=28745c570dd971a5f7ce1e80e09d24ff</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref54"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref54'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">54</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit54" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2017.11.198"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ou, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">In Situ X-Ray Diffraction Investigation of CoSe<sub>2</sub> Anode for Na-Ion Storage: Effect of Cut-Off Voltage on Cycling Stability</span>. <i>Electrochim. Acta</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>258</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1387</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1396</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.electacta.2017.11.198</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D258%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D1387-1396%26journal%3DElectrochim.%2BActa%26author%3DX.%2BOu%26author%3DX.%2BLiang%26author%3DF.%2BZheng%26author%3DP.%2BWu%26author%3DQ.%2BPan%26author%3DX.%2BXiong%26author%3DC.%2BYang%26author%3DM.%2BLiu%26title%3DIn%2BSitu%2BX-Ray%2BDiffraction%2BInvestigation%2Bof%2BCoSe2%2BAnode%2Bfor%2BNa-Ion%2BStorage%253A%2BEffect%2Bof%2BCut-Off%2BVoltage%2Bon%2BCycling%2BStability%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.electacta.2017.11.198&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c20154&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.electacta.2017.11.198&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit54R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">54</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In situ X-ray diffraction investigation of CoSe2 anode for Na-ion storage: Effect of cut-off voltage on cycling stability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ou, Xing; Liang, Xinghui; Zheng, Fenghua; Wu, Peng; Pan, Qichang; Xiong, Xunhui; Yang, Chenghao; Liu, Meilin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">258</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1387-1396</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Owing to their high specific capacity, transition metal chalcogenides (TMCs) based materials attract enormous attentions for energy storage, yet the performance decay obsd. in TMCs anodes are strongly depended on the host material and working conditions.  Here the authors report CoSe2 nanorods as a promising alternative for Na-ion batteries (SIBs), which are fabricated by a facile hydrothermal strategy.  At upper cut-off voltage of 0.4 V, the as-prepd. sample can demonstrate improved sodiation capacity, rate capability, and cycling stability (a high capacity of 386 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1 even after 2000 cycles).  In situ XRD and ex situ TEM measurements were used to study phase transition behavior of CoSe2 nanorods in the initial 9 sodiation/desodiation cycles.  The high electrochem. reversibility of CoSe2 nanorods within the potential window of 0.4-3.0 V is ascribed to that the deep conversion reaction &lt;0.4 V is effectively avoided, thus the vol. expansion and pulverization of CoSe2 nanorods are efficiently suppressed.  It convinces that applying suitable and optimal cut-off voltage is a useful approach to regulate the reactions progress for TMCs anode, improving their cycling and structure stability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoYcwBAdL7-HLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhewmrlm55lWA"> &gt;&gt;                         rightTab-cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium-ion batteries: present and future</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hwang, Jang-Yeon; Myung, Seung-Taek; Sun, Yang-Kook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Society Reviews</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">46</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3529-3614</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Energy prodn. and storage technologies have attracted a great deal of attention for day-to-day applications.  In recent decades, advances in lithium-ion battery (LIB) technol. have improved living conditions around the globe.  LIBs are used in most mobile electronic devices as well as in zero-emission electronic vehicles.  However, there are increasing concerns regarding load leveling of renewable energy sources and the smart grid as well as the sustainability of lithium sources due to their limited availability and consequent expected price increase.  Therefore, whether LIBs alone can satisfy the rising demand for small- and/or mid-to-large-format energy storage applications remains unclear.  To mitigate these issues, recent research has focused on alternative energy storage systems.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as the best candidate power sources because sodium is widely available and exhibits similar chem. to that of LIBs; therefore, SIBs are promising next-generation alternatives.  Recently, sodiated layer transition metal oxides, phosphates and org. compds. have been introduced as cathode materials for SIBs.  Simultaneously, recent developments have been facilitated by the use of select carbonaceous materials, transition metal oxides (or sulfides), and intermetallic and org. compds. as anodes for SIBs.  Apart from electrode materials, suitable electrolytes, additives, and binders are equally important for the development of practical SIBs.  Despite developments in electrode materials and other components, there remain several challenges, including cell design and electrode balancing, in the application of sodium ion cells.  In this article, we summarize and discuss current research on materials and propose future directions for SIBs.  This will provide important insights into scientific and practical issues in the development of SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGot-2IKXj-Q-7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0litO5f6P35Sxw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXkvF2rsbk%253D&amp;md5=cfc7b2d153696dcbded22d954ff06174</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1007/s40820-020-0391-9"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gaddam, R. S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Stabilising Cobalt Sulphide Nanocapsules with Nitrogen-Doped Carbon for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Storage</span>. <i>Nano-Micro Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>12</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">48</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1007/s40820-020-0391-9</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Stabilising cobalt sulphide nanocapsules with nitrogen-doped carbon for high-performance sodium-ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Yilan; Gaddam, Rohit R.; Zhang, Chao; Lu, Hao; Wang, Chao; Golberg, Dmitri; Zhao, Xiu Song</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano-Micro Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">48</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NLAEBV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2150-5551</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nano-Micro Letters</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Conversion-type anode materials with a high charge storage capability generally suffer from large vol. expansion, poor electron cond., and sluggish metal ion transport kinetics.  The electrode material described in this paper, namely cobalt sulfide nanoparticles encapsulated in carbon cages (Co9S8@NC), can circumvent these problems.  This electrode material exhibited a reversible sodium-ion storage capacity of 705 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 with an extraordinary rate capability and good cycling stability.  Mechanistic study using the in situ transmission electron microscope technique revealed that the volumetric expansion of the Co9S8 nanoparticles is buffered by the carbon cages, enabling a stable electrode-electrolyte interface.  In addn., the carbon shell with high-content doped nitrogen significantly enhances the electron cond. of the Co9S8@ NC electrode material and provides doping-induced active sites to accommodate sodium ions.  By integrating the Co9S8@ NC as neg. electrode with a cellulose-derived porous hard carbon/graphene oxide composite as pos. electrode and 1 M NaPF6 in diglyme as the electrolyte, the sodium-ion capacitor full cell can achieve energy densities of 101.4 and 45.8 Wh kg-1 at power densities of 200 and 10,000 W kg-1, resp.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqnPOB01qJKIrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0litO5f6P35Sxw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhs1ehurc%253D&amp;md5=71036c1c7fd5465fedb8c9ec12d8f67a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2017.12.014"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ali, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Asif, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Cobalt Selenide Decorated Carbon Spheres for Excellent Cycling Performance of Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Storage Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>13</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">19</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">28</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.ensm.2017.12.014</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="

                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref6" class="rightTabRefNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit6" data-doi="10.1002/adma.202007262"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Meng, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">CoPSe: A New Ternary Anode Material for Stable and High-Rate Sodium/Potassium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>33</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2007262</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adma.202007262</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">CoPSe: A New Ternary Anode Material for Stable and High-Rate Sodium/Potassium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Feng, Yutong; Xu, Mengzhu; He, Ting; Chen, Bingjie; Gu, Feng; Zu, Lianhai; Meng, Ruijin; Yang, Jinhu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">33</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">16</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2007262</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0935-9648</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The exploration of ideal electrode materials overcoming the crit. problems of large electrode vol. changes and sluggish redox kinetics induced by large ionic radius of Na+/K+ ions is highly desirable for sodium/potassium-ion batteries (SIBs/PIBs) toward large-scale applications.  The present work demonstrates that single-phase ternary cobalt phosphoselenide (CoPSe) in the form of nanoparticles embedded in a layered metal-org. framework (MOF)-derived N-doped carbon matrix (CoPSe/NC) represents an ultrastable and high-rate anode material for SIBs/PIBs.  The CoPSe/NC is fabricated by using the MOF as both a template and precursor, coupled with in situ synchronous phosphorization/selenization reactions.  The CoPSe anode holds a set of intrinsic merits such as lower mech. stress, enhanced reaction kinetics, as well as higher theor. capacity and lower discharge voltage relative to its counterpart of CoSe2, and suppressed shuttle effect with higher intrinsic elec. cond. relative to CoPS.  The involved mechanisms are evidenced by substantial characterizations and d. functional theory (DFT) calcns.  Consequently, the CoPSe/NC anode shows an outstanding long-cycle stability and rate performance for SIBs and PIBs.                         rightTab-cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Dimensional Gradient Structure of CoSe2@CNTs-MXene Anode Assisted by Ether for High-Capacity, Stable Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu Enze; Li Pengcheng; Quan Junjie; Zhu Hanwen; Sun Zhenjie; Chen Lei; Jiang Yang; Wang Li; Chang Yajing; Yu Dabin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano-micro letters</span>

    </div><div class="casAbstract">Recently, abundant resources, low-cost sodium-ion batteries are deemed to the new-generation battery in the field of large-scale energy storage.  Nevertheless, poor active reaction dynamics, dissolution of intermediates and electrolyte matching problems are significant challenges that need to be solved.  Herein, dimensional gradient structure of sheet-tube-dots is constructed with CoSe2@CNTs-MXene.  Gradient structure is conducive to fast migration of electrons and ions with the association of ether electrolyte.  For half-cell, CoSe2@CNTs-MXene exhibits high initial coulomb efficiency (81.7%) and excellent cycling performance (400 mAh g(-1) cycling for 200 times in 2 A g(-1)).  Phase transformation pathway from crystalline CoSe2-Na2Se with Co and then amorphous CoSe2 in the discharge/charge process is also explored by in situ X-ray diffraction.  Density functional theory study discloses the CoSe2@CNTs-MXene in ether electrolyte system which contributes to stable sodium storage performance owing to the strong adsorption force from hierarchical structure and weak interaction between electrolyte and electrode interface.  For full cell, CoSe2@CNTs-MXene//Na3V2 (PO4)3/C full battery can also afford a competitively reversible capacity of 280 mAh g(-1) over 50 cycles.  Concisely, profiting from dimensional gradient structure and matched electrolyte of CoSe2@CNTs-MXene hold great application potential for stable sodium storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcSNIXzBS4qhe5SWdIdmEou5fW6udTcc2ea_3s81a7baCrntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BB2c7pt1KrsQ%253D%253D&amp;md5=603abdedbec7d13e93c9c18e002f0fe1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref9" class="rightTabRefNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit9" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2019.122206"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, X.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, H.         </div><div class="casAbstract">CoSe2 is a potential anode material for Na-ion batteries in terms of their high Na storage capacity and tunable properties.  However, structural degrdn. and unstable interphase during the reversible sodiation and de-sodiation lead to fast capacity decay.  The authors develop a nanocomposite architecture based on CoSe2 nanoparticles embedded in N-doped C matrix with conformal TiO2 coating (CoSe2@NC@TiO2) by using a metal-org. framework-assisted strategy.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Engineering novel electrode materials with unique architectures has a significant impact on tuning the structural/electrochem. properties for boosting the performance of secondary battery systems.  Herein, starting from well-organized WS2 nanorods, an ingenious design of a one-step method is proposed to prep. a bimetallic sulfide composite with a coaxial carbon coating layer, simply enabled by ZIF-8 introduction. Heterostructures exhibit intriguing and significant properties for functional material applications, such as photosensing devices, semiconductor materials, and supercapacitors.  Rechargeable batteries as typical energy-storage devices have drawn widespread attention in the past several decades, on account of high energy d., being low-cost, and ecofriendly.  Prepg. superior active materials is the crit. technol. to ameliorate the electrochem. performance of batteries.  In recent years, the concept of constructing heterostructures for the application of electrode materials has been considered as a promising design approach.  Among all the electrode materials, metal chalcogenides (MCs) have presented excellent properties due to their high theor. capacity based on multielectron reaction.  Herein, the progress on MCs with heterostructures is summarized in terms of various material species and their specific application for several typical battery systems.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Dual ion batteries (DIBs) exhibit broad application prospects in the field of elec. energy storage (EES) devices with excellent properties, such as high voltage, high energy d., and low cost.  In the graphite-based DIBs, high voltage is needed to store enough anions with the formation of anion intercalation compd. XCn (X = AlCl-4, PF-6, TFSI-, etc.).  Hence, it is difficult for graphite-based DIBs to match proper anodes and electrolytes.  Here, an Se/graphene composite is prepd. via a convenient method, and assembled into a dual-ion full battery (DIFB) as anode with graphite cathode and 1 mol/L NaPF6 in EC:EMC (1:1, v:v).  This DIFB has achieved a high discharge capacity of 75.9 mA-h/g and high medium output voltage of 3.5 V at 0.1 A/g.  Actually, the suitable anode materials, such as the present Se/graphene composite, are extremely important for the development and application of graphite-based DIBs.  This study is enlightening for the design of future low-cost EES devices including graphite-based DIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpqej6qI-51gbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh19Wdzq1qeOg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXht1SrsL%252FO&amp;md5=2aa10bfaf42d934de6640795b316ec92</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref15" class="rightTabRefNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit15" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202101137"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bahlawane, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, B.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The past decade has witnessed a rapidly growing interest toward sodium ion battery (SIB) for large-scale energy storage in view of the abundance and easy accessibility of sodium resources.  Key to addressing the remaining challenges and setbacks and to translate lab science into commercializable products is the development of high-performance anode materials.  Anode materials featuring combined conversion and alloying mechanisms are one of the most attractive candidates, due to their high theor. capacities and relatively low working voltages.  The current understanding of sodium-storage mechanisms in conversion-alloying anode materials is presented here.  The challenges faced by these materials in SIBs, and the corresponding improvement strategies, are comprehensively discussed in correlation with the resulting electrochem. behavior.  Finally, with the guidance and perspectives, a roadmap toward the development of advanced conversion-alloying materials for commercializable SIBs is created.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrrNAJqE0vUU7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljFK7TheOna7Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhslyksLjK&amp;md5=ba1adcae9d915929904905f95ab180fe</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref16" class="rightTabRefNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit16" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201706668"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, X.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lou, X.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nano-Micro Letters</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Combining with the advantages of two-dimensional (2D) nanomaterials, MXenes have shown great potential in next generation rechargeable batteries.  Similar with other 2D materials, MXenes generally suffer severe self-agglomeration, low capacity, and unsatisfied durability, particularly for larger sodium/potassium ions, compromising their practical values.  In this work, a novel ternary heterostructure self-assembled from transition metal selenides (MSe, M = Cu, Ni, and Co), MXene nanosheets and N-rich carbonaceous nanoribbons (CNRibs) with ultrafast ion transport properties is designed for sluggish sodium-ion (SIB) and potassium-ion (PIB) batteries.  Benefiting from the diverse chem. characteristics, the pos. charged MSe anchored onto the electroneg. hydroxy (-OH) functionalized MXene surfaces through electrostatic adsorption, while the fungal-derived CNRibs bonded with the other side of MXene through amino bridging and hydrogen bonds.  This unique MXene-based heterostructure prevents the restacking of 2D materials, increases the intrinsic cond., and most importantly, provides ultrafast interfacial ion transport pathways and extra surficial and interfacial storage sites, and thus, boosts the high-rate storage performances in SIB and PIB applications.  Both the quant. kinetic anal. and the d. functional theory (DFT) calcns. revealed that the interfacial ion transport is several orders higher than that of the pristine MXenes, which delivered much enhanced Na+ (536.3 mAh g-1@ 0.1 A g-1) and K+ (305.6 mAh g-1@ 1.0 A g-1) storage capabilities and excellent long-term cycling stability.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Germanium-based materials have been considered as potential anode materials for sodium-ion batteries owing to their high theor. specific capacity.  However,poor cond. and Na+ diffusivity of Ge-based materials result in retardant ion/electron transportation and insufficient sodium storage efficiency, leading to sluggish reaction kinetics.  To intrinsically maximize sodium storage capability of Ge,nitrogen doped carbon-coated Cu3Ge/Ge heterostructure material is developed for enhanced sodium storage.  The pod-like structure of Cu3Ge/Ge-C exposes numerous active surface to shorten ion transportation pathway while uniform encapsulation of carbon shell improves electron transportation, leading to enhanced reaction kinetics.  Theor. calcn. reveals Cu3Ge/Ge heterostructure can offer decent electron conduction and lower Na+ diffusion barrier, which further promotes Ge alloying reaction and improves its sodium storage capability close to its theor. value.  In addn.,uniform encapsulation of nitrogen-doped carbon on Cu3Ge/Ge heterostructure material efficiently alleviates its vol. expansion and prevents its decompn., further ensuring its structural integrity upon cycling.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Research on Na-ion batteries (SIBs) has recently been revitalized due to the unique features of much lower costs and comparable energy/power d. to Li-ion batteries (LIBs), which holds great potential for grid-level energy storage systems.  Transition metal dichalcogenides (TMDCs) are considered as promising anode candidates for SIBs with high theor. capacity, while their intrinsic low elec. cond. and large vol. expansion upon Na+ intercalation raise the challenging issues of poor cycle stability and inferior rate performance.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal selenides have emerged as a class of promising anodes for sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  However, the notorious issues of their low elec. cond. and huge vol. changes during sodium ion insertion/extn. lead to poor cycling stability and inferior rate capability.  In this work, hierarchically core-branched iron cobalt selenide arrays coated with N-doped carbon shell (denoted as FeCo-Se@NC) were rationally designed and synthesized on carbon cloth through a combined strategy of hydrothermal, selenization and carbonization processes.  Benefitting from the designed arrays with simultaneous Fe doping into the CoSe2 matrix and N-doped carbon coating, the optimized FeCo-Se@NC electrode possesses greatly enhanced structural integrity and accelerated ion/electron transfer kinetics.  When employed as a binder- and additive-free anode for SIBs, the FeCo-Se@NC electrode exhibits a high reversible capacity of 532.1 mA h g-1 at 0.05 A g-1, competitive rate capability (193.3 mA h g-1 at 5 A g-1), and good cycling stability (386.1 mA h g-1 after 150 cycles at 0.5 A g-1).         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries have attracted widespread attention for cost-effective and large-scale elec. energy storage.  However, their practical deployment has been largely retarded by the lack of choice of efficient anode materials featuring large capacity and electrochem. stability and robustness.  Herein, we report a durian-inspired design and template-free fabrication of a robust sodium anode based on triangular pyramid arrays of Bi0.75Sb0.25 alloy electrodeposited on Cu substrates.  The Bi0.75Sb0.25 arrays exhibit an appreciable electrochem. robustness for sodium storage, sustaining a reversible capability 335 mAh g-1 at a high rate of 2.5 A g-1 and 87% of the initial capacity over 2000 cycles.  We further demonstrate the applicability of the Bi0.75Sb0.25 array anode in sodium full cells by pairing it with a Na3V2(PO4)3/C cathode.  This full cell achieves a high specific energy of 203 Wh kg-1 (based on both active electrodes).  Such an enhanced performance is attributed to the thorny-durian-like architecture and bimetallic alloy compn.  The pyramid tip induces ion enrichment for rapid charge-transfer reaction, while the alloy design reduces the electrode vol. swelling for stable Na cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqLck-l7_HvOrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li7q9XZ9fzkwg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXht1CltbzO&amp;md5=f310715ed1b7366e17639acccc30dd75</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref27" class="rightTabRefNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit27" data-doi="10.1039/c9ta06273d"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tian, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, X.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hong, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Carbon-Coated CoSe<sub>2</sub> Nanoparticles Confined in N-Doped Carbon Microboxes with Enhanced Sodium Storage Properties</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Due to their high theor. specific capacity, CoSe2-based anode materials have attracted enormous attention for sodium storage.  However, the poor cycling stability and rate capability still hinder their application.  Herein, starting from Co3[Co(CN)6]2 Prussian blue analog microcubes, a facile template-engaged strategy is developed to design and synthesize nanostructured dual-carbon-confined CoSe2 (denoted as DCC-CoSe2) microcubes.  In this unique nanostructure, N-doped carbon-coated CoSe2 nanoparticles are confined in N-doped carbon microboxes.  Benefiting from the desired structural features, the as-synthesized DCC-CoSe2 microcubes exhibit enhanced sodium storage properties in terms of high specific capacity (480 mA h g-1), excellent cycling stability (94.5% capacity retention over 2000 cycles), and superior rate capability (281 mA h g-1 at 20 A g-1).                         rightTab-cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Quasi-reversible conversion reaction of CoSe2/nitrogen-doped carbon nanofibers towards long-lifetime anode materials for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cui, Chao; Wei, Zengxi; Zhou, Gang; Wei, Weifeng; Ma, Jianmin; Chen, Libao; Li, Chengchao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Developing electrode materials with a full conversion reaction is an effective route to break through the capacity barriers, but this goal remains a great challenge.  In this work, we report the synthesis of CoSe2 anodes with a quasi-reversible conversion reaction by uniformly encapsulating CoSe2 nanoparticles in nitrogen-doped carbon nanofibers (CoSe2/N-CNFs).  The space-confined effect of CNFs effectively inhibits pulverization and amorphization of CoSe2 during charge and discharge and thus remarkably ensures the integrity of the crystal structure.  Meanwhile, pseudocapacitive contributed by the size effect of CoSe2 nanodots and excellent cond. due to doped nitrogen heteroatoms give the electrode outstanding electrochem. properties.  When used as an anode, the CoSe2/N-CNFs achieved a reversible capacity of 371.8 mA h g-1 after 500 cycles at 0.2 A g-1.  Even at a high c.d. of 2 A g-1, the discharge capacity of the CoSe2/N-CNFs still reached 308 mA h g-1 after 1000 cycles with excellent rate performance.  The first principles calcns. demonstrate that the heterointerfaces between CoSe2 and nitrogen-doped carbon can significantly enhance the stability of the structure and improve the storage/diffusion capability of Na+.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have drawn much attention due to the abundance and low cost of sodium.  However, electrode materials of SIBs displayed sluggish Na+ diffusivity and fatal vol. expansion, owing to the larger ionic radius of Na+ ions than Li+ ions.  In this work, we built the CoSe2 nanoparticles embedded in graphene nanoscrolls (GNS) as advanced anodes for high-rate SIBs.  The CoSe2/C@GNS anodes exhibited a high reversible capacity of 545 mA h g-1 at 0.2 A g-1. The CoSe2/C@GNS anode also demonstrate ultrahigh rate capabilities (212.5 mAh g-1 at 50 A g-1).  In addn., with a high mass loading (6 mg cm-2), the electrode still displayed a stable capacity (412 mA h g-1 1 A g-1).  The fast electron transfer and Na+ ion diffusion kinetics creates the excellent electrochem. properties, on account of the uniform arrangement of nanoparticles and unique reticular crosslinking structure of CoSe2/C@GNS.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  There is an urgent global need for electrochem. energy storage that includes materials that can provide simultaneous high power and high energy d.  One strategy to achieve this goal is with pseudocapacitive materials that take advantage of reversible surface or near-surface Faradaic reactions to store charge.  This allows them to surpass the capacity limitations of elec. double-layer capacitors and the mass transfer limitations of batteries.  The past decade has seen tremendous growth in the understanding of pseudocapacitance as well as materials that exhibit this phenomenon.  The purpose of this Review is to examine the fundamental development of the concept of pseudocapacitance and how it came to prominence in electrochem. energy storage as well as to describe new classes of materials whose electrochem. energy storage behavior can be described as pseudocapacitive.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrwJEuYlBvPxrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgSqe4zflRTPQ"> &gt;&gt;     </div><div class="casAbstract">High-performance and low-cost sodium-ion capacitors (SICs) show tremendous potential applications in public transport and grid energy storage.  However, conventional SICs are limited by the low specific capacity, poor rate capability, and low initial coulombic efficiency (ICE) of anode materials.  Herein, we report layered iron vanadate (Fe5V15O39 (OH)9·9H2O) ultrathin nanosheets with a thickness of ~ 2.2 nm (FeVO UNSs) as a novel anode for rapid and reversible sodium-ion storage.  According to in situ synchrotron X-ray diffractions and electrochemical analysis, the storage mechanism of FeVO UNSs anode is Na(+) intercalation pseudocapacitance under a safe potential window.  The FeVO UNSs anode delivers high ICE (93.86%), high reversible capacity (292 mAh g(-1)), excellent cycling stability, and remarkable rate capability.  Furthermore, a pseudocapacitor-battery hybrid SIC (PBH-SIC) consisting of pseudocapacitor-type FeVO UNSs anode and battery-type Na3(VO)2(PO4)2F cathode is assembled with the elimination of presodiation treatments.  The PBH-SIC involves faradaic reaction on both cathode and anode materials, delivering a high energy density of 126 Wh kg(-1) at 91 W kg(-1), a high power density of 7.6 kW kg(-1) with an energy density of 43 Wh kg(-1), and 9000 stable cycles.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as a promising energy storage device, but suffer from poor cycling performance.  Here, hierarchical MoSe2 nanotubes were synthesized for the 1st time and demonstrated as a highly durable electrode material of SIBs.  The hierarchical nanotubes consist of few-layered MoSe2 nanosheets with an expanded (002) interlayer spacing of 1.00 nm (54.8% expansion).  The growth of hierarchical nanotubes is a result of oriented attachment and Ostwald ripening effects.  As a robust Na host material, the MoSe2 nanotubes featuring hierarchical organization, hollow interiors, and interlayer expansion are beneficial for (1) lowering diffusion energy barriers and facilitating fast Na+ insertion/extn. reaction kinetics, (2) accommodating vol. changes upon sodiation/desodiation, (3) preserving structural and morphol. stability, and (4) improving electronic cond. by in situ C modification.  By controlling the cut-off voltage of 0.5-3.0 V with an intercalation mechanism, the MoSe2 nanotube electrode shows highly stable cycling performance and delivers a reversible discharge capacity of 228 mAh/g after 1500 cycles at a high c.d. of 1000 mA/g.  This work demonstrates the best cycling performance to date of MoSe2-based anodes for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoj6cQOT7qzKLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh_jVKymxUGNw"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition-metal selenides have captured sustainable research attention in energy storage and conversion field as promising anodes for sodium-ion batteries.  However, for the majority of transition metal selenides, the potential windows have to compress to 0.5-3.0 V for the maintenance of cycling and rate capability, which largely sacrifices the capacity under low voltage and impair energy d. for sodium full batteries.  Herein, through introducing diverse metal ions, transition-metal selenides consisted of different compn. doping (CoM-Se2@NC, M = Ni, Cu, Zn) are prepd. with more stable structures and higher cond., which exhibit superior cycling and rate properties than those of CoSe2@NC even at a wider voltage range for sodium ion batteries.  In particular, Zn2+ doping demonstrates the most prominent sodium storage performance among series materials, delivering a high capacity of 474 mAh g-1 after 80 cycles at 500 mA g-1 and rate capacities of 511.4, 382.7, 372.1, 339.2, 306.8, and 291.4 mAh g-1 at current densities of 0.1, 0.5, 1.0, 1.4, 1.8, and 2.0 A g-1, resp.  The compn. adjusting strategy based on metal ions doping can optimize electrochem. performances of metal selenides, offer an avenue to expand stable voltage windows, and provide a feasible approach for the construction of high specific energy sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqdgjjIFBgG4bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh_jVKymxUGNw"> &gt;&gt;
